X-UIDL: 9d85f7c903f051dbe2f21a1c9491dda6

From: Linus Akesson <lairfight@softhome.net>

In accordance with the prophecy, Chris Seward uttered:

> From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

> Hi,

> My StrICQ just says 'going online' at the top of the window and then
> does nothing, If i open the register UIN window then my number
> will appear and i can send people messages etc.

> But then after about 50 seconds it goes offline?

> Any ideas?

Great, then it isn't just me having that problem after all. It's a rather
peculiar bug in stricq, and the workaround is to open one of its windows
(preferably the log window, hit Amiga-4 to open it) every 10 seconds or so.
This is very inconvenient, but de facto the only way to stay online.

You don't have to close the window before re-hitting Amiga-4, not even
deactivate it. It's like stricq falls asleep, and you have to keeep hitting
that key combination to keep it awake. (Much like I'm feeling now.. yawn)

Linus

   - Linus Akesson ------------------------- http://linusworld.cjb.net -

Hello Chris,

On 31-Aug-99, Chris Seward wrote:
> From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>
> 
> Hi,
> 
> My StrICQ just says 'going online' at the top of the window and then
> does nothing, If i open the register UIN window then my number
> will appear and i can send people messages etc.
> 
> But then after about 50 seconds it goes offline?
> 
> Any ideas?
> 

What TCP stack are you using? If it is Miami you must be using 2.1p at
least or it will do what you are talking about. You might want to read
the faq and it will tell you about these things. Also you might want to
subscribe to the stricq list at :

majordomo@owlnet.net

put     subscribe stricq-list       in the body of the mail

It only gets a few mails each day and there are some helpful people
there.

Doug's stricq page is at http://www.owlnet.net/amiga/stricq

Hope this helps

Kenneth

X-UIDL: d58b89ace85f054cf8ea9593a971fc2b

From: Jack York <jyork@voyager.net>

Hello Don

On 31-Aug-99, Don and Lynn Benson wrote:
> From: Don and Lynn Benson <dlbenson@psnw.com>
> 
> Hi Jack
> 
> On 31-Aug-99, Jack York wrote:
>> From: Jack York <jyork@voyager.net>
>> 
>> Hello,
>> 
>> Has anyone had any experience with inkjet refil kits? Do they
>> work without causing problems? Is there a better way to go?
>> 
> 
> I have used refils in the past with my HP550C printer and they
> worked out okay. The black worked much better than the color.
> With the HP the kit came with a way to drill a hole in the top of
> the cartridge and simply fill  the cart. They furnished a plug
> for the hole. Okay, but messy! I did it over the kitchen sink
> after learning my lesson. Working carefully was an absolute
> necessity. NO rushing the job.
> 
> Color carts. were another matter. One kit I tried `popped' the
> top of the cartridge off. Another drilled 3 holes. The 3 hole
> version was inadvisable. The problem is that the space above the
> 3 color tanks is open. So if you fill a color too fast it spills
> over into the adjacent color. You have to fill it so slow that
> you can go crazy. With the popped top you can see what you are
> doing, but it isn't any faster. Also the colors are different
> from the manufacturer's colors. So if you have calibrated your
> color printing it will be off.
> 
> I have not tried the kits with any other kind of printer.
> 
> I got my color kits from MEI/Micro Center. They also have lower
> priced cartridges for some printers. They have a web site:
> 
> http://www.mei-microcenter.com
> 
> They also have a 800 #: 1-800-634-3478
> 
> Hope this helps.

Yeah it does.  Just the sort of information I was looking for.  I don't
want to cause myself grief to save a few dollars.  I would hate for one
of those plugs to come loose and cause damage.

Thanks Don.

Jack

Just wanted to be clear on one thing. The plugs were never a
problem.

One thing I neglected to mention was that there was a tape to put
over the bottom vents while you filled the cart. HP carts needed
to be pressurized with a little syringe like pump that was
included. Later kits required that you let the cart. sit for 15
minutes to stop any dripping present. Once they were filled they
were great. In fact, I liked their ink better than the original.

----- Don

Subject: [just-amiga] Jim Collas Resigns
X-UIDL: f8440de42625cec22d97dbe179e40505

From: "Chris Green" <chrisgreen@insightonline.clara.co.uk>

This hot off the wires from ZDNet

Chris Green
Technical Editor
Computing



Collas out as Amiga president

Top exec gone after less than eight months at the helm of Gateway
subsidiary.

By Charles Cooper, ZDNN
September 1, 1999 11:39 AM PT

Jim Collas has resigned as president of Amiga after less than nine months on
the job.

It was not clear why Collas left the post. A spokesman for the company said
Collas had resigned to pursue personal interests. Amiga said it had promoted
vice-president and chief operating officer, Tom Schmidt, to fill the
vacancy.

Separately, Collas registered to sell 118,000 shares of Gateway's common
stock, according to forms released Wednesday by the Securities and Exchange
Commission.

The departure of Collas comes less than a month after the company
orchestrated a high-profile coming-out party for the unit, which is a
separate subsidiary of Gateway.

Gateway (NYSE:GTW), which paid about $13 million to acquire the rights to 47
Amiga patents, is attempting to revive the once-popular computer brand.
Collas and other executives involved in the project had indicated interest
in developing Internet-related products based around Amiga technology.

Collas, who held a variety of management posts during his seven years at
Gateway, had eagerly pressed company CEO Ted Waitt and was subsequently
granted the top job at Amiga in January.

He also urged Waitt to let him run Amiga as a separate company.

Before joining Amiga, Schmidt worked as a general manager for Allied Signal,
running one of the company's business units. He was not immediately
available for comment.

Subject: [just-amiga] Digital Camera as a Webcam?
X-UIDL: 7be472f5667a6f5ddfb6de5401854aed

Hi All,

Does anyone know if its possible to use a Digital Camera as a webcam
and if it is then I guess you'd need an extra serial port in the blanking
plate space, ie, one for your internet connection and the other to

Subject: Re: [just-amiga] Digital Camera as a Webcam?
X-UIDL: 7e0d8d1efccc6d1376dcc6595ad2cffc

From: "Oliver Roberts" <oliver.roberts@iname.com>

Hi Chris,

On 02-Sep-99 22:08:57 BST, Chris Seward wrote:

> Does anyone know if its possible to use a Digital Camera as a webcam
> and if it is then I guess you'd need an extra serial port in the blanking
> plate space, ie, one for your internet connection and the other to
> transfer the pictures.

Yep, you'll need two serial ports.  Personally, I use my Surf Squirrel
for my modem and stick the digicam on my A1200s internal serial port.

> Is there any Amiga webcam software out there that can do this type
> of thing?

Well - if the software you use with the camera supports ARexx, it
is relatively to knock up a short script to act as a webcam - i.e.
the script tells the software to take a picture, and then save it to
the ram disk, for example.  Then, in the script, you can put a little
something together to upload it to your webspace or whereever.  Stick
it all in a loop to execute every 30 seconds or something, and you've
got a webcam :)  Of course, things are even easier when the digicam is
connected to the computer which is actually hosting the website in
question :)

Subject: [just-amiga] [digital-images-news] Digital Images Update (fwd)
X-UIDL: 07671e371680b37c196917c76a269109

From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

Hi All,

It seems Digital Images have back out the door.

I am slightly annoyed by this because yet we have see nothing from
them either but promisses and now they act as if they saved the
Amiga in the first place.

Surely they should test the water before backing out, no?

*** FORWARDED MESSAGE ***
  Original author: Stuart Walker
  Written on: 03-Sep-99
*** Beginning of forwarded message ***

To Amiga users worldwide,

Due to recent announcements and problems with Amiga, Digital Images
regrets
that we will be suspending all AmigaMCC projects including Sabrina
Offline.
Space Station 3000 and Wipeout 2097 will be released as planned, but we
will
be suspending all other Amiga developments until further notice.

Everyone behind Digital Images has enthusiastically supported the Amiga
through the good times and the bad times. But with the recent troubles
with
Amiga, the entire team has unanimously decided to suspend all Amiga
developments (with the exception of Space Station 3000 and Wipeout 2097).
We
regret to have to take these measures, but Digital Images cannot afford
to
spend time, resources and money developing for a computer which now, as
it
seems may never appear.

We hope that everybody reading this understands our position as this is
the
last thing that any of us would ever have wanted to do, but Amiga have
made
promise after promise that something would appear, but it has not. 

We deeply regret this decision, but it is a final measure that has to be
taken. We wish that we wouldn't have to go this far, but we now have no
other option - it is the last thing that any of us wanted to do. We would
appreciate it if everybody understood our position and wouldn't send
e-mails
of anger and abuse. We have done everything in our power to avoid this,
but
it just isn't possible. 

If the Amiga does indeed rise again, which we hope it does, we will
return.

We hope that you will enjoy our upcoming releases of Space Station 3000
and
Wipeout 2097.

If you do have any questions or queries concerning this announcement,
please
e-mail info@digital-images.demon.co.uk

We thank you all once again for your loyal and devoted support.

Kind Regards,

Stuart Walker
Digital Images


------------------------------------------------------------------------

*** End of forwarded message ***

 On Thursday September 02 1999, Chris Seward said to All:

 CS> Does anyone know if its possible to use a Digital Camera as a webcam

Should be possible - I'm sure the camera software has ARexx so you can
take and pull in an image when you want one. Of course, it also depends how
long it takes to download images from the camera..

 CS> and if it is then I guess you'd need an extra serial port in the
 CS> blanking plate space, ie, one for your internet connection and the
 CS> other to transfer the pictures.

Erm..

If you connect via modem on the same machine, you would need two
serial ports.  It really doesn't matter where the second port is ;-)

 CS> Is there any Amiga webcam software out there that can do this type of
 CS> thing?

You really don't need any dedicated web cam software.  All you'd be
doing is updating a file every so often.

Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: text/plain
Subject: [just-amiga] Amiga show in a central UK location possible?
X-UIDL: 4971b000c8c239ca8e47a1f54a7e4add

From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

Heylo!

I was just thinking that for a few years now the main Amiga show of
Great Britain has been held in London which may seem like a central
place but really is not. London is a complex place with high prices
and for some it is too far to travel.

The people who ran this years WoA surely covered their expense
otherwise they would not have run the show. One major factor of
expense to cover is the cost of renting a venue in london which
I suppose could be even double or triple the price of a 'hall' or
'area' in another part of the country depending on what size
you rent.

Then I hear people moan that it is not a good location for them, me
included, but nothing is ever done. The people who ran WoA are
just normal people like you and me and surely one of us could
start planning an Amiga show in a location to be more reasonable
to people.

Manchester, Liverpool and Birmingham are all major places with
many more included so why doesn't someone have an idea to
start a show up. I'm sure lots of people will help out and show
support, you could even gather interest to see which location
will pull the biggest crowds and then go and look for a suitable
place to rent with a big enough size to make it a 'real' show. Not
just a school sports hall because that screams User groups
show, but a professional show like the WoA or as professional
as it could be.

I'm sure many of you in a small group could form a little team to
make something like this and if we throw some ideas around then
surely something could get going?

Damn it, i'd even help whether I could attend or not just for the
fun of things.

I could set up a vote page of certain locations to see which
place people are most likely to travel to which is easy for them.

Come on everyone, does anyone have any ideas on this?!

Toodle Pip!
-- 
Chris Seward - Editor, Amiga Information Online

> From: Lorens Johansson <SnorsleX@Home.se>

> 
>>>> Try changing servers....telling us the version number.....if it worked
>>>> before....if you have installed any new hardware ,software etc etc.
>> 
>>> Ver : 0.1480
>> I'm using 0.1408 which was the last version (from then on they are betas
>> with the chat function disabled)
> 
> The latest v is 0.1504, and it has working SINGLE chat!!

Yeppers:) In fact, working 2-way chat (single) has been working since 0.1493
(at least) from my personal experience :) Multichat is partially functional
too. For example a 3rd person can enter the chat but you get a second chat
window with them, they can see you in their single window, but you must type
to each of them seperately as if in 2-way chat. It's odd but it works if you
really want to try it and have plenty of screen real estate. The new chat
windows are quite large unless you set the toolbar.mcc prefs for STRICQ to
images only.

this year's WoA. I believe that they already have some plans to move
from London. They have gained a lot of experience from this year's show,
and I'm sure the next one they organise will be even better.
>

> many more included so why doesn't someone have an idea to
> start a show up. I'm sure lots of people will help out and show

> will pull the biggest crowds and then go and look for a suitable
> place to rent with a big enough size to make it a 'real' show. Not
> just a school sports hall because that screams User groups
> show, but a professional show like the WoA or as professional
> as it could be.

Next year's WoA will either be too large for amateurs to arrange, or
too small for even a school sports hall. It all depends on what
happens at Amiga now Jim has gone.
>
> I'm sure many of you in a small group could form a little team to
> make something like this and if we throw some ideas around then
> surely something could get going?

If you could raise about 20,000 pounds to pay for all the things
that need arranging before the show, I'm sure that would help a lot...

> Damn it, i'd even help whether I could attend or not just for the
> fun of things.
>
> I could set up a vote page of certain locations to see which
> place people are most likely to travel to which is easy for them.

I don't think this is a good idea. WoA location has been discussed to
death on other mail lists, and at the end of the day people's preferences
don't usually match commercial realities.

>>> Does anyone know of an T-Shirt printers who will maybe do small
>>> amounts of prints, good quality at a cheap price.
>>>

> to do this.  I have TurboPrint but don't see an option for this.
> Can you explain to me what I am missing?

If you go to Turbo print prefs then to the graphics page / section ,
you will see in the bottom right a tick box for negative & mirror .

The mirror is the one you are looking for .

You can get some good results , but remember to use white or 
pale tee shirts .

Subject: [just-amiga] T-Shirt printing thread
X-UIDL: 097d2d369f1c8e872280cb86fcf6c449

From: "Tony P. Parr" <tony@merlin.net.au>

Greetings All...

Recently various people asked and answered about T-Shirt printing. I offer
the following limited information, based on my own experience:

Original from Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

> Does  anyone  know  of  an  T-Shirt  printers  who will maybe do small
> amounts of prints, good quality at a cheap price.
>
> Or does anyone know of any T-Shirt printers that are good :)?

My answer (previously sent privately)

I  own a Canon and have access to an HP_Deskjet and Epson Stylus Color IIs
and  there  are kits including TShirt transfer sheets etc., available that
work on all the above.

I  have  not  used  them  for a while and going from memory, you print the
horizontally  flipped  image (or whatever) on the special sheet, then iron
on to TShirt. Of course if there's no text, there's no need to flip.

Once again from memory, I think there was a special ink cartridge too.

They worked a treat on the 3 or 4 TShirts I did some years ago.

The  only  one  I  see  now is about 3 years old and unless my Son is very
grubby,  it has been washed (as per directions in the kit) many times with
only minor fading.

> Thanks  for  your  help. I may look into this, although I only own an
> old  Star  LC200  which  is  not  up to the job. It would probably be
> cheaper for me just to find a place that could print the t-shirts.

If  you  follow this route, I think you will have to save your image as an
color  separated  image on to a PC or MAC formatted disk. Printing outlets
don't  seem to have heard of the Amiga (uninformed, benighted people), and
won't be able to load the image. A lot more work for the desired result.

> But thanks again, I may have a go when I get a new printer!

Do  not even attempt using a dot-matrix (pin) printer. The results are, to
say the least, 'orrible. Here in OZ, for example, one can buy the cheapest
Canon  bubble-jet for as low as $A139, complete with bi-directional cable,
and  software  (unfortunately PC oriented). I'm on a low, fixed income and
even I can afford one.  8-)
__________________________________________________________________________

> Do  you  have  PageStream3.x?  If  so, all you need do is to flip the
> object(s) horizontally on the page, then print.

>> Yes I do but unfortunately the things I want to print were generated
>> by ImageFX and PageStream won't load them.

Why  anyone  would  use  PageStream as their printing program of choice is
beyond me. Why not load the image and print direct from the art program to
the TShirt printing media?

(As an aside, why anyone would use PageStream, period !!)

Please,  no endless mails informing me of the error of my ways and I don't
know what I'm talking about.  8^Q

>>> Jack,  I  am  sure ImageFX has the ability to mirror and image. There
>>> are  a  number of other GRFX programs that do this with images. Also,
>>> PgS  prints all my pics from ImageFX and every other graphics program
>>> I can find. Exactly what format are the pics in?

ImageFX can load/save in many formats including: BMP, ILBM, GIF, JPEG, PCX
and 8 or 24 bit and a plethora of others.
__________________________________________________________________________

> It would seem all I need to do it to be able to print in reverse but
> I don't see how to do this.  I have TurboPrint but don't see an option
> for this. Can you explain to me what I am missing?

>> If  you  go to Turbo print prefs then to the graphics page / section,
>> you will see in the bottom right a tick box for negative & mirror.
>>
>> The mirror is the one you are looking for.

Correct re: mirroring in TurboPRINT, but, unless you're printing text, why
would you want to flip the image, unless you wanted a highlight printed on
a particular side... (read as "overly fussy")   8-)

The vast majority of drawing programs on the Amiga will flip images.

>> You  can get some good results, but remember to use white or pale tee
>> shirts.

Not  necessary.  Choose/change the colours in your image with care and you
can  save  your image for printing on any coloured material. I printed all
my  attempts on black. Don't forget, you're not printing direct to TShirt,
but to special media that you iron-on to the material later.

TIP: the background colour of your image must be the transparent colour in
     whatever program you use to draw/alter/save the image.
__________________________________________________________________________

FYI...  PhotoGenics loads/saves in many formats and can flip images in any
direction and can do some fantastic image manipulation.

PersonalPaint will do most things asked of a GFX program. Very powerful.

Below is an overview of THE proggie for converting GFX formats and it does
much, much more. This is what GfxLab24 is capable of, very impressive, I'm
sure you'll agree:

 GfxLab24 OverView
 -----------------

   GfxLab24 is a 24-bit and bitmap image processing program. It runs
   under AmigaOS 3.0 or higher. Here are some of its features:

   - Loading :

        - IFF24
        - IFF 2 & 8 - HAM6 - HAM8
        - JPEG
        - TARGA
        - PNG (bitmap & RGB)
        - Any picture DataType (GIF, BMP, PCX,... etc.)

   - Saving :

        - IFF24
        - IFF 2-8bit, HAM6, HAM8
        - GIF (specs GIF87a et GIF89a)
        - Jfif (JPEG)
        - TARGA.
        - PCX
        - PNG (bitmap & RGB)

   - Display the picture from 2 to 8 bitplanes + HAM6/8, with or
     without a fixed palette (13 halftoning/error diffusion modes).

   - Fast previewing window. Operators are applied in REAL TIME !

   - 24 processing operators:

        - Colour To Gray
        - Mask Filter
        - Brightness
        - Scale (reduction/enlargement by % or with height/width in
          pixels)
        - Crop
        - Emboss
        - Sketch
        - Negative (on any of the three RGB componants)
        - Rotate
        - Bicolor (Turn picture to black and white. 9 halftones.)
        - Flip (horizontal or vertical)
        - Visual Aspect (modify the display and pixels ratios)
        - Quake (horizontally or vertically)
        - Disperse pixel (setting the radius and the probability)
        - Convolve (Applying/Editing/loading/saving matrices library
          of convolution)
        - Remove isolated pixel
        - Quantize palette (Quantizing/loading/saving palette)
        - Balance filter (modify gamma,sin,brightness,contrast)
        - Fade (fading between two pictures)
        - Whirl
        - Brush copy (with transparent color)
        - Text
        - Noise (white or coloured)
        - Mosaic

   - Built-in Virtual Memory management, available on ANY
     Amiga computer, even WITHOUT MMU, and fully adjustable.

   - Intuition 3.0 interface, and preference management.

   - ARexx Port allowing automatic processing. Some ARexx scripts are
     provided as example.

   - Best of all, GfxLab24 is FREEWARE !!

There is also a neat little proggie called Transition which does single or
batch conversions of image file formats.

Hope this is of some help to those budding Warhols, Turners or Picassos.

Cop 'U Later... Tiny

> 

Turns out the problem appears to be in TurboPrint.  The printout is
a mixture of text and graphics.  When printing in the higher densities
the text is partly shifted.  That is to say, the top part of the first
letter is printed at a certain position while the bottom part of that
same letter is printed about 1/4 inch to the right.  I turned off the
mirror option and reversed the text in PageStream before printing.  
Turned out fine.  The only problem now is judging the contrast and
brightness levels.  Printing on plain paper gives a different look
than printing on the transfers.  And each time I change it, another
sheet of transfer is trashed.  Is there a better way?


> Lara Croft pics on light coloured denim jakets ( for my 2 girls not me ;-)

Sure...if you say so. ;)

Subject: [just-amiga] NEVER register a .co.uk domain
X-UIDL: 86055939c695cd404c331369d55741fe

From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

Hello interested readers!

I'd just like to warn everyone NEVER to register a .co.uk domain
because they give you so much trouble.

I suggest going for a US one like .com/.net/.org because these
are simple to move and trouble free.

I have been trying to get the DNS servers of aio.co.uk moved because
I have a new place to host the AIO website. It has been going on
for around 2 months and they still refuse to change the DNS servers.

The site is registered to someone else because he did this for me
because at the time he could host it but he emailed them and they told
him that he would need to fax them an 'official' company headed
paper requesting the change of the DNS servers. He did this and
still it has not moved.

For this I appologise for the sorry state the AIO site is in with some
times it being up and sometimes not and also for not letting me get
on with the site updating the bits that need updating on a regular
basis.

The last word of warning, *NEVER* register a .co.uk

Toodle Pip!
--

I expect some of these to continue, but under Gateway rather than
Amiga.

Subject: [just-amiga] == THE PHOENIX PLATFORM CONSORTIUM ==
X-UIDL: efb5446586467791a78612d508df1d0b

From: Kenneth Craig <kwdjc@wf.net>

Hello all,
    Thought you might be interested in this:


== THE PHOENIX PLATFORM CONSORTIUM ==

We are pleased to announce the acceptance of provisional charter for
the Phoenix Platform Consortium.

Phoenix signatories believe it is time to place our destiny back in
the hands of folks who understand what the Amiga is all about. You
will notice members of the original Jay Miner team within our ranks.

Unlike other new entities we will not field questions from newsgroups,
mailing lists, or in email, nor will we be erecting a marketing facade
to false hopes. Results and honest direction are our mandate.

The Phoenix Platform Consortium will assume responsibility for aid and
recommendation for reference platforms for the Amiga users who wish to
upgrade their present Amigas, as we establish an open migration path
to a new platform. That platform will in spirit and in feel be a new
Amiga experience while incorporating and surpassing the features found
on the desktop elsewhere today.

More information will be posted when we have facts to present. Please
do NOT email the participants in curiosity. We ask for your patience
in this matter. Please respect the wishes of the participants named
below. There is much to do and we have just begun.

As information becomes available it will be posted on mailing lists,
newsgroups, and at the following website: http://owlnet.net/phoenix/
which will be up shortly. This announcement is freely repostable.

Thanks, from the Phoenix Platform Consortium, currently:

about it. You also get 25mb of web space even if there website says 10mb. The
hosting costs nothing.

Subject: [just-amiga] Executive Update response.
X-UIDL: 5b8afe71d17d411068aa20ba1c33ce06

From: Mike Cardwell <mickeyc@ukonline.co.uk>

*Reply to quotes from the Executive Update (14/09/99)*

N.B. If you read the whole thing, and have followed Amiga for the last
few months, then you'd understand why I seem to over react a little 
here. I don't know what Schmidt had been smoking when he wrote it, but
he needs to come back down to Earth.

> First, I hope you'd agree that Amiga was never about a box.  It was 
> never about an operating system either. Sure those things were part of
> what made the original Amiga great, but at its heart, Amiga was simply
> about a better way.

Rubbish. The Amiga is a computer, with a brilliant operating system,
easy to use, and easy to expand. Amiga is not a concept. I didn't buy my
Amiga for the community, I bought it for the computer.

> Amiga was ahead of its time.  Amiga promised to change the world.  It 
> ran against conventional wisdom and was better than anything out there
> at the time.  In fact, we could all argue that it's still better than
> anything out there.

Could we? What about Amiga Emulation on a Pentium 3? Get the best of
both worlds. Maybe the emulation isn't as fast as running Amiga software
on a real PPC Amiga. But how is the Amiga going to keep up, if Amiga is
not going to be developing hardware? Does this mean the MCC has been
dropped? Sounds like it to me.

> But to limit Amiga to just one box, one product, one OS, is to keep 
> Amiga from ever seeing its full potential.

I don't understand what you're talking about. What are you saying that
Amiga is? It's a computer, it can come in many varietys. I just expected
that Amiga it's self would actually develop one, rather than leaving it
to third parties.

> So why not have Amiga running on every type of device imaginable, on 
> top of every other OS out there?

This insinuates that you are classifying Amiga as a piece of software.
If not an OS, then what?

> So long live Amiga, but if you think that Amiga was just a box, you've > missed the point.

Bo****ks! Many people are expecting, a brand new spanking Amiga. One
with all the current advantages, but with a decent hardware spec. Amiga
has turned it's back on us. What's going to happen to OS5 with it's
Linux kernal. Has everything we've been told about just been dropped?

> Thomas J. Schmidt
> President & C.E.O.

I guess G4/QNIX are our only hope now. But will any third party company
take the risk of developing an Amiga with the specs we were promised, at
such a low price? I don't think so. :(

P.S. Sorry to be so negative. It's just so frustrating to listen to so
many promises, start to believe them, and then realise they were all
lies. Please don't demean this list by flaming me publicly, if you 
disagree. I do however expect there'll be more response to this, in the
list.

--

On 13-Sep-99, you wrote:

> If Gateway/Amiga have ditched plans for a new Amiga why are they

Well everyone else has done it why not add another to the line. No
one really knows what is going on except whoever is at Gateway and
Amiga and i guess they don't know either ;)

It wouldn't make sence for Gateway to just use the name because it
would hold nothing for us Amiga users slapped on another box which
is just an internet-tv setup. I don't even think those Internet-TV
jobbies do very well as computer prices drop and everything that
is anything comes bundled with a modem there is no use for them.

If they want to make something else then they could use any name
because Amiga (the name) does not hold much respect these days
apart from us Amigans so it would not give anything a head start.

Why would they pay for the rights and just use a name, they can
make a new name which would be free and they wouldn't exactly
use the 'old' Amiga technology so basically they will have wasted
a few million dollers.

I for one am never going to use a PC because my Amiga does alot
of things I want it to do. Some people say they can't see themselves
using the Amiga in 5 - 10 years but we've been using basically
the same Amigas from 1994 so why not? I don't think I can see myself
using anything else. I'm not even sure i'd want to use a new Amiga
if it ever came out because it would be 'nothing' like our current
Amigas and maybe thats just our problem, we want something the
same but want it to change which is never going to happen. Its
stick with the Amiga or get a PC, I don't think i can ever see any
other way, its been like that for so long i'm used to it.

From: "P.Steadman" <stead@reaperman.demon.co.uk>

hello all "Amiga users"

this is my first message on just-amiga cos i'm the quiet type but i just had
to have a rant and the lads at work look at me like some sort of looney
when i ramble on about corporate betrayal, broken promises, that relay just
blew up, er no sorry they expect me to say that. anyway you get the picture
you probably get similar looks especially if youre a window dresser and you
say the relay one.  anyway here i go. 

*/rant begin/*

Amiga inc. have always had secret partners, can't say too much, loose lips
sink chips etc. now they say that they will not be producing hardware, but
will become a software company, working with "business partners". 

Who the hell are these "business partners"?. 
are they always the same business partners or are they new business partners
each time?. 
why wont they tell us who these people are? 

On the face of it, Amiga inc. seem to have a talent for choosing bum
companies for business partners and they must be aware of the ultimate
"bum"ness of these companies or they wouldn't be keeping them out of sight.
the only company they have announced a partnership with, QNX, was dropped
when it looked like being a possible success story. hopes dashed yet again,


look at the record of this company, 

leak story to amiga press that PPC will be the next amiga processor, allow
sufficient time for programmers and hardware manufacturers to get PPC
projects underway then, just at the right moment, announce to the world
that the new amiga processor is a secret but we'll give you a clue, its not
the PPC, go extremely quiet for a long time,(hinting about secret deals),
announce deal with QNX, subtly hint at PPC version of OS5 QNX style, wait
for PPC market to pick up again, announce end of deal with QNX and great
new deal with with that well known secret company, transmeta hinted at, the
boss quits(never a good sign),the newly ex boss offloads 100,000 shares in
company(thats probably a really bad sign), finally announce that the new
processor has finally been selected and it will be non-existent, this
seemingly magical device operates purely on a mental level its
specifications are quoted as the highest number you can think of +1. well,
we can dream can't we. 

apparently, for seven years now i have been operating under some delusion
that i was using a computer, silly me, it was a philosophy i was typing on,
no, it was more than that it was an ideal, a better way, ha, these people
are all leading us down the garden path right the way to the (bill) gates,
now they dont even conceal the fact, 

well, from now on i couldnt give a toss what they say, if they produce
something worthwhile i might just look it over, but it might just be
running on a fast pentium in which case we may as well all go out and buy
one tomorrow (Gateway do some nice ones, co-incidentally), maybe run an
amiga emulator or something, and if the emulator for the best computer that
NEVER existed comes along from amigasoft,(system requirements:- Windows 95,
USS Enterprise main computer) we can all get ourselves into an Amiga frenzy
and the boys at gateway can pat themselves on the back after the success of
their two year strategy

long live Amiga, thats what they say to us, but what did they license first?
the OS for amiga forever, the UAE package for PC use. think about it.
parent company- major PC manufacturer allows small offshoot company to
produce superior computer systems with the ultimate aim of destroying
parent company's market. sound feasible, nope , the new amiga system must
operate on parent company's machines or it will not be produced. the secret
partners would appear to be .....

it is now clear that we have been cut adrift in an open boat, so to speak, i
for one am glad that the waiting is over (dont believe them again) and the
money i have put aside for the new amiga can be put to good use upgrading
my miggy even further, the better way is already at my fingertips it may
not run at supersonic speeds compared to a PC but i reckon i can produce
quicker with an amiga cos its easier to use(thats my philosophy). and
there's one thing the PC will never have, AmiNet, 

remember the days when we didn't have this type of software or that picture
format didn't work, you cant run this bloated game on an amiga cos they
aint got hard drives, no sound cards outside of big box machines, endless
lists of limitations, look about you now there aint much we cant do with
the miggy, obviously 1.3 Amiga 500 systems are going to struggle a bit but
there is plenty of life left in the old A1200 yet just keep giving it the
silicon injections 8)

*/rant end/*

i leave you with a lighthearted biblical thought, draw your own parallels, 

the bible predicts that at the end of the world, the beast will rule the
earth, only 144,000 people will be saved and go on to live in paradise,
these 144,000 people will be the only ones not to bear the mark of the
beast, 

how many Amiga users did you say there were ? 

144,000 ?

Could God be an Amiga user 8)

144,001 ?


                                     Keep on "Amiga"ing
                                                        Stead




P.S. do you resent "That firm" christening us "Amigans" cos i bloody well
do. Personally i'm not ready to give up being an "Amiga User" just yet and
if i ever do decide to give up my miggy i may as well just go and commit
macintosh 8).

From: Colin Wenzel <colstv@hotkey.net.au>


It is just an cmos invertor chip that turns the horizontal & vertical
sync upside down.  It draws the power directly from the supplies
available on the video port,  I dont know where you get one,
but any tv technicial could throw one together on a piece of
veroboard for you, in half an hour....

Subject: Re: [just-amiga] Amiga Format drops again!
X-UIDL: 127cb1a7125349a4671a1066c02f4c64

From: Eric Chernoff <eric@chernoff.org>


> From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net> 
> new Amiga is released. I will not be using a PC because i have no use
> for it, I can give a 95% promise that AIO will still be going in a
> 
> There is not alot more you will beable to do with a computer so the
> Amiga does what I want, the only things i miss is some internet

This is all so true!  I am so tired of hearing people say that because of
AmigaOS's age and lack of mainstream support that it is somehow less
functional than a PC.  Boulderdash!  I *need* my Amiga to do the things I
do.  No PC is as versitile, stable, and outright fast as an Amiga (yes, I
know that raytracing proves me wrong, but I don't raytrace.)  

I don't know if those who are about to buy a PC know what is going to
happen to them.  They will pay a good price to get quite a bit of power
and software, and it will be fast and stable at first.  That is, assuming
you don't put any more software on, but Amigans are hackers, so they will
install more software, and with each new program, the machine will
decrease in speed by 2-5% or so.  But it should level off somewhere around
45% od its original speed and stability.

Both mainstream Web browsers are quite unstable -- illegal memory
operations mostly.  Java is decent, but adds no functionality whatsoever,
and RealVideois unusable with a modem connection.  Also, it doesn't behave
too well if *any* other apps are running.  Also, emulating an Amiga is not
satisfactory at all:  It is incompatible with many legacy progs, it
crashes constantly, and it's incredibly slow!  It's still fun, but just
not like having an Amiga (I bought Amiga Forever 2.0)

The biggest problem with PCs is that nothing is free.  There is no Aminet
with giftware and freeware and cheap shareware.  Everything costs money.
Download.com is decent, but nothing--no-thing--is freeware.  Developers go
into the Amiga for the Love of the Machine and to make cool stuff happen.
Other developers go into the Windows market to make money.  Hence, stuff
is outrageously expensive.  Except for Web Browsers, of course, but they
come with more advertising that the Home Shopping Network.

The hardware, while newer and a little more stable, flatly sucks.  IDE is
pitiful next to the vanilla SCSI in a 3000, and try adding cards to a PC.
IRQs are such pains in the butt, I don't even want to start.  

The bottom line is that PCs look cute in the store, they even behave well
the first 3 days at home, but after that they turn to crap.  I know
many/most of you know this, but I just few that those folks who are
interested in switching to PCs need to hear this again.

The closest OS to AmigaOS in my opinion is Sun Solaris, but it's hard to
use.  Sun stations are awesome toys, and there is free Solaris for Intel
boxes.  The best hardware in the world right now is coming from Apple,
though, those G4 towers are super fast, super easy to upgrade and super
nice.  Both Suns and Apples are really pricey, though.  But you get what
you pay for.

The only way I would ever recommend a PC is if gaming is your number one
priority.  That's really what PCs are good at.  Otherwise, MS Word is
worse than Final Writer, IE/Netscape are slower and more crash-prone than
AWeb, and the networking sucks, and on and on.

If you still want a PC, then I recommend Dell.  Their hardware sucks the
least.  Avoid Compaqs and home-brews.  Also avoid Toshibas.  That's just
asking for it.

My experience is with a Dell Demension PC with 450Mhz, an HP Kayak at
300Mhz and several Toshiba laptops.  I have an A3000 with a CyberStorm
MkIII, which makes everything else feel like crap.

Just my opinion, flame at will.

-Eric

On 18-Sep-99, Chris Seward wrote:

Try UKOnLine, and dial up using the Easynet numbers.
UKonLine are free and are basically the same company as Easynet, so you can
use the Easynet news servers etc for free :-))

To find a real dial in number go to
http://www.easynet.co.uk/easynet/everywhere/search.html and put in a place
name that is as near/far to/from you as you need.

Cheers.

From: "Jonas Thorell" <jonasth@bahnhof.se>


Eric Chernoff wrote:

> This is all so true!  I am so tired of hearing people say that because of
> AmigaOS's age and lack of mainstream support that it is somehow less
> functional than a PC.

That depends on what you want to do, doesn't it? One thing
for example: I make my living by being a network administrator, mainly
with Windows NT being the server-OS. How do I add the client-based server
tools I need to the Amiga? That's right, I can't. Or how about this:
I need to be able to access MS-Access databases every now and then, also
a non-starter on the 'Miggy. Or how about saving MS-Word files (and don't
mention RTF-files since the RTF-filters in MS-Word and FinalWriter/Wordworth
aren't always compatible...)?

Don't get me wrong here, I really like the Amiga (I don't use the word
love for inanimate objects) but some things just cannot be done with it
as it is now (and vice verse).

>Boulderdash!

Great game isn't it...

> do.  No PC is as versitile, stable, and outright fast as an Amiga (yes, I
> know that raytracing proves me wrong, but I don't raytrace.)

Well, depends on how the PC is configured. Mine doesn't crash more
than my Amiga does. Win98 on the PC and AOS 3.1 on the other. Some
patches running on both too. And WindowsNT is even less crash-prone,
although it isn't fool-proof (no OS is).

> I don't know if those who are about to buy a PC know what is going to
> happen to them.  They will pay a good price to get quite a bit of power
> and software,

The hardware is cheap compared to a Amiga-system. The software is
priced waaaay over the top.

> and it will be fast and stable at first.

And later, if you know what you're doing.

> That is, assuming you don't put any more software on, but Amigans are
hackers, so
> they will install more software, and with each new program, the machine
will
> decrease in speed by 2-5% or so.

A certain truth in it, due to the registry. It's not ALL that bad though,
some software doesn't expand the registry at all or just minor and thus
have a smaller impact.

> Both mainstream Web browsers are quite unstable -- illegal memory
> operations mostly.

Unfortunately true. Or fortunately perhaps...

>Java is decent, but adds no functionality whatsoever,

Depends. Most Java-stuff is quite useluss but it can be put to good use.

> and RealVideois unusable with a modem connection.  Also, it doesn't behave
> too well if *any* other apps are running.

Strange that I routinely have some 10 programs running. That's the
programs I constantly have a use for (that is, at work) and the computer
isn't crawling. At home I don't have the need to have as many programs
running at the same time.

> Also, emulating an Amiga is not satisfactory at all:

It most certainly is not. It works but that's about it.

> The biggest problem with PCs is that nothing is free.  There is no Aminet
> with giftware and freeware and cheap shareware.  Everything costs money.

Not really. There are freeware and giftware software there too. Besides,
if you don't need the latest versions some PC-mags do the same thing
CU used to do: covermount older versions.

> The hardware, while newer and a little more stable, flatly sucks.  IDE is
> pitiful next to the vanilla SCSI in a 3000,

On the other hand, the SCSI in the 3000 is good for a plain SCSI-II
interface. Add a decent SCSI-card to the PC and there's a stalemate
on that point.

> and try adding cards to a PC.

Usually quite easy, although the Amiga is far superior on that
account. But the PC cards are generally speaking superior in the
price/perfomance ratio. I can get a TNT2 Ultra card for less money
than a PicassoIV and the latter is as slow as AGA in comparison.

> The bottom line is that PCs look cute in the store, they even behave well
> the first 3 days at home, but after that they turn to crap.  I know
> many/most of you know this, but I just few that those folks who are
> interested in switching to PCs need to hear this again.

Why switch? Use both computers, i.e. best of both worlds.

> The closest OS to AmigaOS in my opinion is Sun Solaris, but it's hard to
> use.

I haven't used Solaris much but how different to any other Unix-variety
can it be? A good X-Window environment can do wonders.

> Sun stations are awesome toys,

Not very cheap though...

> boxes.  The best hardware in the world right now is coming from Apple,
> though, those G4 towers are super fast, super easy to upgrade and super
> nice.

If you don't mind the clumsy operating system.

> priority.  That's really what PCs are good at.  Otherwise, MS Word is
> worse than Final Writer, IE/Netscape are slower and more crash-prone than
> AWeb, and the networking sucks, and on and on.

Which part of the networking?

> If you still want a PC, then I recommend Dell.  Their hardware sucks the
> least.  Avoid Compaqs and home-brews.  Also avoid Toshibas.  That's just
> asking for it.

Agreed completely! Also avoid IBM Aptivas, especially the earlier
models.

> My experience is with a Dell Demension PC with 450Mhz, an HP Kayak at
> 300Mhz and several Toshiba laptops.

I have experience with just about every laptop ever been released by IBM,
several compaq laptops and about 13-14 different models of stationery
machines from several brands (IBM, Compaq, Dell, Toshiba and Gateway).
Oh, and some really heavy duty server-only models too, including one
DEC-Alpha server.

>I have an A3000 with a CyberStorm
> MkIII, which makes everything else feel like crap.

Ah, just what I have...almost. MKII but what the...

/Jonas

On 18-Sep-99, Chris Seward wrote:

> 
> Issue 129 is now out (to subscribers) and the new figure is,
>

> lost over 1000 readers.

Remember that they've been really pushing the subscriptions over the past few
weeks/months though. IIRC, the subscriptions are not included in this figure,
though you'd need to verify this with Future Publishing. So this figure may
account for a great deal of that drop. 

FWIW, I still buy AF and have been every issue since late 1990. But I can
understand that with more and more people going on-line that they don't feel
the need to buy it as the information is woefully out of date compared to
that on the net. That's not a critisisum of AF, it's the same with any mag
and deadlines that have to be met. There's also the percieved cost of the mag
for what it offers that other sources don't. Personally I'm in the lucky
position that 6 quid every four weeks is small change.  

Though as I've said the news is of no interest I still buy it for several
reasons. My top three below.
 

(1) Reviews
(2) Tutorials, I got a great deal out of the one that Neil Bothwick did on
HTML.
(3) Readers Stuff. A lot of which never appears anywhere else.

From: Eric Chernoff <eric@chernoff.org>



> From: "Jonas Thorell" <jonasth@bahnhof.se>
> for example: I make my living by being a network administrator, mainly
> with Windows NT being the server-OS. How do I add the client-based server
> tools I need to the Amiga? That's right, I can't. Or how about this:

Have you tried Samba?  That makes the Amiga both a client and a server on
the NT network?  It can't really handle PDC stuff yet, but my wife has my
Amiga's larger disk mounted as H: on her PeeCee.  There are two versions
of Amiga Samba:

http://www.kampsax.dtu.dk/~rask/Samba/
and
ftp.logicalline.de/pub 

I just downloaded the second one tonight and will try it out later.

Samba is definitely a cool Unix port to have.  As is Amiga QMail and Amiga
Apache.  No NetShow of course or NetMeeting, and that is important.

> I need to be able to access MS-Access databases every now and then, also

I haven't looked too far into the ODBC world on an Amiga.  I understand, I
run MySQL on my Sun Sparc Classic and I wish my Amiga could access that.
There is a MSQL port for the Amiga, and it may be helpful.  Still, this is
a point I will gladly concede.

> a non-starter on the 'Miggy. Or how about saving MS-Word files (and don't
> mention RTF-files since the RTF-filters in MS-Word and FinalWriter/Wordworth
> aren't always compatible...)?

Very true.  The only real way to use an Amiga for you would be to have
ShapeShifter insalled and run Office 98 for the Mac.  Having a built-in
Mac would give you access to mainly mainstream tools, but you would only
have to use it when necessary.

I understand the need to take files to and from work.  I operate with
ASCII myself or do my word processing on my PowerBook from work.  I still
stand by the fact that FinalWriter is a great litte word processor and
more than most people really need.

> Well, depends on how the PC is configured. Mine doesn't crash more
> than my Amiga does. Win98 on the PC and AOS 3.1 on the other. Some

I really find that a little hard to believe.  My Amiga did have a crashing
problem until I replaced the 8520's and the Buster.  Then the 060 addition
sealed it.  It stays on 24/7 (runs www.chernoff.org) and crashes maybe
once a week on a bad piece of downloaded shareware (bad habit).

> The hardware is cheap compared to a Amiga-system. The software is
> priced waaaay over the top.

I read somewhere that Amigas run $5 software on $3,000 machines while PCs
run $3,000 software on $5 machines.  Kind of funny.

> > and it will be fast and stable at first.
> And later, if you know what you're doing.

I have yet to see anyone who has no had stability problems with their PC.
I am not saying I don't believe you have it under control, but I have
never seen it with my own eyes.

> > decrease in speed by 2-5% or so.
> A certain truth in it, due to the registry. It's not ALL that bad though,
> some software doesn't expand the registry at all or just minor and thus

It should *never* be that case IMHO.  What I detest most about the
Registry is that it is almost impossible to get an unwanted program's
dropping out of the registry once its in.  It's also next to impossible to
get all of the dll's out too.


> > and RealVideois unusable with a modem connection.  Also, it doesn't behave
> > too well if *any* other apps are running.
> Strange that I routinely have some 10 programs running. That's the
> programs I constantly have a use for (that is, at work) and the computer
> isn't crawling. At home I don't have the need to have as many programs

And this is video?  I agree that the RealAudio runs very smooth, and it's
all I really want when working (broadcast.com is awesome), but video is
still on the way, I feel.

> > The biggest problem with PCs is that nothing is free.  There is no Aminet
> > with giftware and freeware and cheap shareware.  Everything costs money.
> Not really. There are freeware and giftware software there too. Besides,
> if you don't need the latest versions some PC-mags do the same thing
> CU used to do: covermount older versions.

I will take your word on it.  I still believe that given a good Amiga with
the full OS, you can download most of the apps you need for free.  Not
all, but most.

> > The bottom line is that PCs look cute in the store, they even behave well
> > the first 3 days at home, but after that they turn to crap.  I know
> > many/most of you know this, but I just few that those folks who are
> > interested in switching to PCs need to hear this again.
> 
> Why switch? Use both computers, i.e. best of both worlds.

It's seem an extraordinary number of people talk about the fateful day
when their Amigas go into the closet and the PC takes the desk.  People
seem tired of being in the weird crowd, especially since they aren't being
rewarded for it.  I agree with you, but I think many folks don't look at
it that way.

> > The closest OS to AmigaOS in my opinion is Sun Solaris, but it's hard to
> I haven't used Solaris much but how different to any other Unix-variety
> can it be? A good X-Window environment can do wonders.

A lot.  It is very, very slick, and very fast.  My Sparc Classic has a
mere 32 megs of RAM and a 50Mhz CPU, but it runs everything I throw at it
beutifully.  Is it as fast as my Amiga?  Not even close!  But it is very
compatible, scalable, and professionally done.  Sun has made a fine
product in Solaris.

I use Linux at work for our file/web server, and it does the job, but it
really doesn't compare to our Ultra 5 which is 166 slower (500 versus
333).  Of course Suns are RISC and the Linux boxe is CISC, but Solaris has
a strong air of legitimacy that Linux still lacks.  Plus the Common
Desktop Environment is the best Unix windowing system yet.  It's smooth
and still fast.

> > Sun stations are awesome toys,
> Not very cheap though...

True.  Computers are a situation where you get what you pay for.  Cheap
equipment is available, but not very good.  Suns are over most people's
budget, including mine, but used Suns can be found for the same prices as
used Amigas, most are cheaper.  Sun themselves has a used equipment
program, but you'll have better luck on Usenet.

> > boxes.  The best hardware in the world right now is coming from Apple,
> > though, those G4 towers are super fast, super easy to upgrade and super
> If you don't mind the clumsy operating system.

Now that's an interesting statement coming from an NT guy!  MacOS is the
most inefficient, non-multitasking OS I have seen, but its also the most
elegeant when it comes to the user interface.  Everything about using my
Mac is a true joy, and the last word I would say about it is "clumsy."  In
fact, I contend that Windows 95/98/NT attempts to be MacOS but fails
miserably.  It wants to make computers easy but really complicates matters
because Windows can't handle the behind-the-curtain stuff like MacOS.
With MacOS, you don't need to know anything about the guts, but with
Windows, you really do, because if the GUI technique goes wrong, then
fixing the problem will take an MCSE to begin to understand.

> > AWeb, and the networking sucks, and on and on.
> Which part of the networking?

The controls are missing.  I am using Miami Deluxe, and really, nothing
compares to it.  MiamiDx is the best networking package on any computer
anywhere, anytime.  It is the only GUI-driven package that puts more power
in the hands of the user than a command-line package.  Plus, it actually
fills my A2065, and I have never seen a PC fill an Ethernet card, 10 or
100 mbs.  Granted, most Amigas can't use 100 mbs cards, but I hope that
will change someday.

I am glad we agree and disagree on so much.  You sound like someone who
has learned to love NT somewhat, and I can respect that.  NT is far better
than Windows 9x, but it is a toy compared to Solaris or Linux.  A lot of
folks feel that NT is the thing to use because Unix boxes require more
time and effort, but the busiest, most stressed out folks I know are NT
admins.  My Unix machines can run years without being touched.

The Amiga lacks a lot of features, but so does every OS on the market.  I
feel that the Amiga doesn't lack the most important features, and so I
stick with it.  Perhaps if my machine is still at 50mhz when others run at
10Ghz, I will have to switch.  But truthfully, Windows boxes are as slow
as ever, and my Amiga gets faster with age (or maybe I am going crazy.)

-eric

From: "Jonas Thorell" <jonasth@bahnhof.se>

Eric Chernoff wrote:

>> for example: I make my living by being a network administrator, mainly
>> with Windows NT being the server-OS. How do I add the
>> client-based server tools I need to the Amiga? That's right, I can't.

> Have you tried Samba?

Not on my Amiga, which unfortunately lacks a network-card but I've
seen it in action. It works, albeit not the easiest thing to configure.

> That makes the Amiga both a client and a server on
> the NT network?  It can't really handle PDC stuff yet, but my wife has my
> Amiga's larger disk mounted as H: on her PeeCee.

I don't think it will work as long as no-one makes tools for altering
the user/mail/etc databases on the PDC/BDC. The UserManager For Domains
and ServerManager at the very least needs to exist.

Come to think of it, a workaround might be possible if I set up
a telnet-daemon on the NT-server and telnet in and use calcs to alter
user-rights. Everything can't be done that way though (:

> Samba is definitely a cool Unix port to have.  As is Amiga QMail and Amiga
> Apache.  No NetShow of course or NetMeeting, and that is important.

I don't know how important the latter two are, actually. Never met anyone
that has used them. The Amiga-ports of QMail and Apache, while they are
good, I wouldn't trust the Amiga as a server on the Internet. It's too
vulnerable without protected memory and user-rights (MuFS isn't good
enough).

>> I need to be able to access MS-Access databases every now and then, also

> I haven't looked too far into the ODBC world on an Amiga.

Is it at all possible?

> I understand, I run MySQL on my Sun Sparc Classic and I wish my Amiga
could access
> that. There is a MSQL port for the Amiga, and it may be helpful.  Still,
this is
> a point I will gladly concede.

I'm by no means a SQL-expert but from what I've heard, the Amiga-port is
lacking things the other ports does have. Now, where is that Oracle8 port...

> Very true.  The only real way to use an Amiga for you would be to have
> ShapeShifter insalled and run Office 98 for the Mac.  Having a built-in
> Mac would give you access to mainly mainstream tools, but you would only
> have to use it when necessary.

I did that for a while but decided it wasn't worth the effort. Especially
since there are 3 PC's standing next to me as well...

> I understand the need to take files to and from work.  I operate with
> ASCII myself

I cannot do that unfortunately. Too many damn macros in some of them (:
And not by my choice either.

> or do my word processing on my PowerBook from work.

Probably the best solution.

> I still stand by the fact that FinalWriter is a great litte word processor
and
> more than most people really need.

I agree. It's a great little program. Too bad it won't use TrueType fonts
though. Or can FW97 do that? I'm a little behind the times there and
have a later version.

>> Well, depends on how the PC is configured. Mine doesn't crash more
>> than my Amiga does. Win98 on the PC and AOS 3.1 on the other. Some

> I really find that a little hard to believe.  My Amiga did have a crashing
> problem until I replaced the 8520's and the Buster.

Well, both of them crashes occassionally but not too often. Mainly when
I try out some new software that wasn't as well-behaved as it should be.

> Then the 060 addition sealed it.  It stays on 24/7 (runs www.chernoff.org)
and
> crashes maybe once a week on a bad piece of downloaded shareware (bad
habit).

Too much when it comes to a machine that stands as a server. Then again,
that's
unavoidable with an unprotected OS.

> I read somewhere that Amigas run $5 software on $3,000 machines while PCs
> run $3,000 software on $5 machines.  Kind of funny.

Not too far from the truth either.

> I have yet to see anyone who has no had stability problems with their PC.
> I am not saying I don't believe you have it under control, but I have
> never seen it with my own eyes.

I didn't say I have never had it but it's been stability itself for the
last couple of months. It probably will develop a problem at some
time...most likely because some silly program insists on installing
a older version of some .DLL without asking me.

>> A certain truth in it, due to the registry. It's not ALL that
>> bad though, some software doesn't expand the registry at all or just
>> minor and thus

> It should *never* be that case IMHO.

No, it shouldn't. Unfortunately, it is.

> What I detest most about the Registry is that it is almost impossible to
get an
> unwanted program's dropping out of the registry once its in.  It's also
next to
> impossible to get all of the dll's out too.

What, you don't like working with Regedit and regedit32?? ;-)

The worst problem with the registry IMO is that it makes the entire OS so
unstable. One entry in the registry gone wrong and you may have to reinstall
the OS. And for some things, you *need* to manually alter the
registry. There is no other way.  Some (read: a lot) of Microsofts
proposed solutions explicitly states that you need to alter the registry.
Which I really do not like to do. The /bin/etc solution in *IX is a
better approach. Or the ENVARC: way.

>> Strange that I routinely have some 10 programs running. That's the
>> programs I constantly have a use for (that is, at work) and the computer
>> isn't crawling. At home I don't have the need to have as many programs

> And this is video?  I agree that the RealAudio runs very smooth, and it's
> all I really want when working (broadcast.com is awesome), but video is
> still on the way, I feel.

Not over the 'Net but I've had the MediaPlayer or WinAmp playing away
without
getting interrupted while having a bunch of other programs running. For
Video
over the 'Net, it's not really the PC's fault: it's the damn slow
connections
and congestions everywhere that makes it stutter. I don't know how well
or bad RealVideo is programmed so that's just a guess.

> I will take your word on it.  I still believe that given a good Amiga with
> the full OS, you can download most of the apps you need for free.  Not
> all, but most.

Very true. But I don't like that I have to buy a god-damn CD-ROM filesystem.
True, there is one in AOS 3.1 and some on Aminet but they're worthless in
comparison to AsimCDFS or CacheCFS (IMHO that is).

>> Why switch? Use both computers, i.e. best of both worlds.

> It's seem an extraordinary number of people talk about the fateful day
> when their Amigas go into the closet and the PC takes the desk.

Well, I've seen it happen...and I guess most people here has too. It's gone
to the point where people actually asks me when I'm going to throw mine
into the bin. The day it dies of old age and I can't find replacements,
that's when.

> A lot.  It is very, very slick, and very fast.  My Sparc Classic has a
> mere 32 megs of RAM and a 50Mhz CPU, but it runs everything I throw at it
> beutifully.  Is it as fast as my Amiga?  Not even close!

Not surprising. A OS with real VMM, MP and Multiuser will be slower than
one which has not, and your Amiga had a better Mhz number too. True, Sparcs
are RISC so not directly comparable.

> But it is very compatible, scalable, and professionally done.  Sun has
made a fine
> product in Solaris.

Compaqs Tru64 isn't bad either. Requires a Alpha-server though which aren't
cheap.

> I use Linux at work for our file/web server, and it does the job, but it
> really doesn't compare to our Ultra 5 which is 166 slower (500 versus
> 333).

I don't know if this is true or not but from what I've head that is
because Solaris can handle a whole lot of more threads per process
than Linux. Linux is supposed to be around 20/process and Solaris
1024/process,
should make a difference to say the least.

> True.  Computers are a situation where you get what you pay for.  Cheap
> equipment is available, but not very good.  Suns are over most people's
> budget, including mine, but used Suns can be found for the same prices as
> used Amigas, most are cheaper.  Sun themselves has a used equipment
> program, but you'll have better luck on Usenet.

I might try to find one...I'll also see if I can convicne my employer
that the old VAX-Mainframe in the basement would be better of at home...

>> If you don't mind the clumsy operating system.

> Now that's an interesting statement coming from an NT guy!

Maybe, also a matter of personal taste.

> MacOS is the most inefficient, non-multitasking OS I have seen,

Indeed. The TOS/GEM combo on the AtariST is up there too.

> but its also the most elegeant when it comes to the user interface.
> Everything about using my Mac is a true joy, and the last word I would say
about it is
> "clumsy."

Well, just a small list of things I find utterly annoying:

1. The lack of responsiveness.
2. When something crashes the computer can freeze completely
   with no option besides turning the power off.
3. The Data/resource gibberish filesystem which makes it a nightmare
   trying to open documents where the original creator isn't available.
   Usually involves using ResEdit.
4. No good scripting utility a la WSH or Arexx (AppleGuide or Hypercard
doesn't
   cut it).
5. No command prompt whatsoever.

I have used Macs extensively before and everytime a beginner asks how to
remove
a disk from the diskdrive..."Drag it into the trashbin". "No, I don't want
to erase
what's on it"...

> In fact, I contend that Windows 95/98/NT attempts to be MacOS but fails
> miserably.  It wants to make computers easy but really complicates matters
> because Windows can't handle the behind-the-curtain stuff like MacOS.

True. It tries too and in some cases it succeeds perfectly, in other cases
well the less said than better.

> With MacOS, you don't need to know anything about the guts, but with
> Windows, you really do, because if the GUI technique goes wrong, then
> fixing the problem will take an MCSE to begin to understand.

Good thing I am one then.

>> Which part of the networking?

> The controls are missing.

True. On the other hand, if you use NetBEUI you don't need any...but you
don't want to use that. The thing that annoys me the most is that all
the network-parameters aren't in one place. No, no. You need to alter
things at several places.

>I am using Miami Deluxe, and really, nothing
> compares to it.

I have just used ordinary Miami and if Deluxe only delivers half of
what it promises it is one heck of a TCP/IP stack.

> fills my A2065, and I have never seen a PC fill an Ethernet card, 10 or
> 100 mbs.

Me neither, but sometimes you could be fooled into thinking it becuase
of the speed (or lack thereof).

>Granted, most Amigas can't use 100 mbs cards,

Can any Amiga do it?

>but I hope that will change someday.

It's supposed to. I don't know how far RBM has progressed with it but they
claim a 100 mbs Ethernet-addon is in the works for their IOBlix.

> I am glad we agree and disagree on so much.  You sound like someone who
> has learned to love NT somewhat, and I can respect that.

I wouldn't go that far. It's got more than its share of silly bugs and
oversights but all in all, it's usable and most likely the best desktop OS
for networks there is. It's familiar for the users and therefor easier
for them, which cuts down on support issues but doesn't elliminate them.
As you say, Linux and Solaris are better OS but I think they're better of
being "just" the server-OS.

And don't get me started on Windows2000. Someone shoot the people
responsible
for that piece of crap, although some things in it are nice.

> NT is far better than Windows 9x, but it is a toy compared to Solaris or
Linux.

True.

> A lot of folks feel that NT is the thing to use because Unix boxes require
more
> time and effort, but the busiest, most stressed out folks I know are NT
> admins.

Hey! Have you looked at my schedule lately?...Truth being told, the servers
aren't the problem. The workstations are since you never can trust the
users enough. And I have turned off many options so they cannot screw up
that
many things. Sad part is, it's impossible to prevent it all together since
if
you do you effectively cripple them so they cannot do their job. It's a
tough
balance act.

> The Amiga lacks a lot of features, but so does every OS on the market.

Yep. Most things I miss when infront of another OS is generally
speaking some of the Amigas applications, not some aspect of the
OS although that comes into play as well. I do find myself missing
my very customized workbench though...I simply cannot put my finger
on what it is that makes the Amiga so special that I don't want to
get rid of it.

/Jonas

Hi All,

Well by now most of you are probably bored by my rants at AF and
its staff but i'm going to rant anywa ;) Thats not to say that I don't
like AF because I have actually just taken out a 12 month subscription
with them, if they'll still be around in 12 months is another matter
altogether.

The first knowledge of Paul Cavanagh was when he called my up
saying he was reviewing Wasted Dreams for AF, as I am the UK
Distributer for the game I offered him the advice and then see
the review which gives the game 72% overall. Not wanting to sound
bias but even if I wasn't the UK Distributer I would certainly
give it a hell of a lot more than that as most of the people who
registered it did.

Before I'd actually seen the review a person from one of the
leading Amiga software suppliers, VERY well known who will
remain nameless also told me that they had their doubts about
Mr. Cavanagh but thats all I will say on that matter :-)

This month I see the Gremlin Collection receive 36%. Firstly
I do not condone piracy but some of these games on that CD
are not available anymore so how the heck does he expect
them to appear on the CD. Its alright people today saying
that you should buy the games but say when a company has
gone bust and the game doesn't exist anymore to buy, what
do you do? well people are left with one solution.

I notice he didn't complain about AF putting a full game of
Stunt Car Racer on the CD a few issues again and the reply
to a persons letter about it was that the Aminet also had
it, they call THAT and excuse?

I think Mr. Cavanagh was expecting a CD full of playstation
games because the games on the CD are some of the all time
greats, Gremlin was a market leader back then and probably
still would be on the Amiga. Zool was one of the a1200 launch
items and looking through the list of old scores from past
magazines that they display at the top most got over 80%.

Is Mr. Cavanagh up for the job? Why didn't AF employ an
Amiga fan and not someone who packed up their Amiga
well over 2 years ago?

Toodle Pip!
--

Subject: Re: [just-amiga] Changing IBrowse fonts
Content-Type: text/plain
X-UIDL: 062a70d7adafb96a1be21383d4715158

From: Darren Stevens <daz@sunhawk.u-net.com>

On 19-Sep-99, Jack York wrote:
>From: Jack York <jyork@voyager.net>

>Hello,

>How do I change the font in IBroswe that is used to display
>text in the window?  No matter which of the three fonts I change
>in the MUI settings, the text remains very small.
Thats because you are changing the fonts MUI uses for windows and gadgets.
To change the fonts for HTML displays you must open the 'General...'
settings window and choose the fonts tab from there. You'll see 3 sets of
fonts to change there, each corresponding to a different HTML style.

Hope this helps..

Darren

Subject: [just-amiga] Amiga - any future?
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
X-UIDL: d60313ad3f066c5b2979c5150b0171ea

From: Frank Bunton <bunton@acay.com.au>

I quote below the final words from
Open Letter to the Amiga Community
September 17, 1999
From
Thomas J. Schmidt
President and CEO
Amiga, Inc.

> In summary, we are continuing to focus our
> resources on setting software standards for
> the coming generation of Internet appliances.
> We are not planning to offer hardware devices,
> but will work with hardware manufacturers who
> want to license our technology. As far as
> offering next-generation Amiga systems, we
> are open to talking to companies who want to
> offer such a product. 

To be honest, if I were a hardware developer, I don't think I would be
too enthused about developing the hardware when Amiga Inc. seem to be
only interested in "Internet Appliances"!

To my way of thinking, the only way a new Amiga computer would be able
to take off again would be for Amiga Inc. to produce the new Amiga
computer and back it up with solid advertising. Nothing will take off
without solid positive advertising from Amiga Inc. itself. Their current
comments only seem to reinforce our opinions that they are only
interested in the  "Internet Appliances" side of things.

--

try and has the backing.

Do you think the lack of software will hurt sales. I have not
heard anything about any software for it, yet.

> Amiga, Inc.
> 
>> In summary, we are continuing to focus our
>> resources on setting software standards for
>> the coming generation of Internet appliances.
>> We are not planning to offer hardware devices,
>> but will work with hardware manufacturers who
>> want to license our technology. As far as
>> offering next-generation Amiga systems, we
>> are open to talking to companies who want to
>> offer such a product. 
> 
> To be honest, if I were a hardware developer, I don't think I
> would be too enthused about developing the hardware when Amiga
> Inc. seem to be only interested in "Internet Appliances"!
> 
> To my way of thinking, the only way a new Amiga computer would
> be able to take off again would be for Amiga Inc. to produce
> the new Amiga computer and back it up with solid advertising.
> Nothing will take off without solid positive advertising from
> Amiga Inc. itself. Their current comments only seem to
> reinforce our opinions that they are only interested in the
> "Internet Appliances" side of things.
> 

-----Don

Greetings all...

Not sure if this is the right place to ask, but here goes...

Can someone advise me (in plain English please) what purpose do AmiTCP and
AmiFTP and similar programs serve?

I often see them mentioned in MLists and a friend has all sorts of assigns
and extra lines in his user-startup/startup-sequence to run these programs
and complained about the problems he had setting them up.

When  I  asked the above question he couldn't give me an answer, just that
he'd been advised to have these running before he went online on the 'net.

I run Miami, YAM and iBrowse and get mail of all kinds from all around the
world. With iBrowse I go to http and ftp sites and never have any problems
connecting  and  D/Loading  HTML files, LhA, LZX or DMS archives, nor do I
have any problems attaching files to my emails.

So... any easily understood answer would be appreciated.

I am having an on-going debate re: attaching files to emails. 

Except  for  one  person,  in  all  the dozens of mails I've received with
attachments  the attachment has been of base64 type and the YAM manual and
other  texts  I've  read lead me to believe this is the norm these days as
the  encoding is smaller, (ergo, faster in transmission) and more reliable
than uuencoding. The way I have my system set up (button in DOpus) it also
seems easier to decode base64 files.

Again, an easily understood answer on this subject would be of help.

Thanx to all in advance.

Cop 'U Later... Tiny

Anything Miggy related...

>Can someone advise me (in plain English please) what >purpose
do AmiTCP and
>AmiFTP and similar programs serve?

Well, AmiTCP does the same a Miami; it dials up your ISP, and
sets up a TCP/IP connection to allow you to communicate.
AmiFTP allows you to download files from Aminet etc., and allows
you to upload too- its bloody good at it too.

>I often see them mentioned in MLists and a friend has all >sorts
of assigns
>and extra lines in his user-startup/startup-sequence to >run
these programs
>and complained about the problems he had setting them up.

Wouldn`t know about that.

>When  I  asked the above question he couldn't give me an >answer,
just that
>he'd been advised to have these running before he went >online
on the 'net.

Unless you have another magical way, it *would* be useful.
(You could always use Miami though, which you do)

>I run Miami, YAM and iBrowse and get mail of all kinds >from
all around the
>world. With iBrowse I go to http and ftp sites and never >have
any problems
>connecting  and  D/Loading  HTML files, LhA, LZX or DMS >archives,
nor do I
>have any problems attaching files to my emails.

Good for you- you won't be able to upload much, though.

<Snip>

>Thanx to all in advance.

No problem.

>Cop 'U Later... Tiny

  Sandy Brownlee

>   If in doubt, put some tape over that area. That'll prevent any shorting
> out.

What kind of tape would you recommend ?? Any kind?
