From: lnbolch@freenet.edmonton.ab.ca
To: lnbolch <teamamiga@thule.no>
Reply-To: teamamiga@thule.no


>                                          ....  Back in the days when C=
> had organized a group to interface to federal organizations they showed
> up at one of the computer/electronic exhibits sponsered by NASA at the
> Langley research center.  They displayed the A3000 and the A3000UX. Just
> about the only comments I heard were along the lines of "What's a toy
> company doing at a computer show?"

L Bolch:-

No question that was the attitude in the late 80's. The interesting thing
is that games are largely driving computer evolution now. With the
perspective of a decade, people are realizing that much of what is new and
slick on the PC and Mac was being done with our "game machine" in 1985. 

The insult of 1989 has become the supreme compliment of 1999. I would love
to be conceited enough to think that nVidia, Matrox, ATI, 3Dlabs and all
are developing boards for my 3-D excesses, but those billions are being
spent to corral the games players first. We enjoy the fall-out.

The budget for a game rivals that of movies as does the profit. Look at
all the press coverage surrounding Sega and Sony's new consols. Games are
big business now and getting a LOT of respect.


We tend to think that the on-line community is the whole Amiga community.
We are just the loud ones who get noticed, and may well be just the small
but visible tip of a rather large iceberg.

I am constantly running into people involved with other systems who have
nothing but respect and admiration for what Amiga pioneered. A honcho from
Tandem told me that throughout his company, Amigas were pervasive - the
engineers regarded them as micro-mainframes, using them much as you do, as
a programming sketch-pad at home. 

A lot of people programming in the Windows market, started with Amigas and
still have them at home. Had lunch with one last Saturday. The company he
works for is releasing a pretty major application this week and he was the
architect. He is still an enthusiastic member of AmiCUE.

Many of the AmiTrix group work for other system companies as their day
jobs, but still develop and distribute Amiga products. They just completed
the legal paper work for the browser in OS3.5, and it should now be in
Haage & Partner's hands. As of last Thursday, Dale and Yvon had pretty
much wrapped up the coding.

Amigas have been and ARE STILL BEING USED throughout the whole television
and video industry - at least in North America. Probably 99% of the
professionals working in the CG/FX production houses began their careers
or caught the love of CG/FX on Amigas and speak with great nostalgia about
them. NewTekniques Magazine is still loaded with Amiga features, news and
ads. Many who work with SGI and NT machines still have their Miggies at
home. 

A whole 'nuther community - perhaps larger even than this on-line bunch. A
big difference is that they don't - and never did - regard the Amiga in
the way that the religious cast does. It was a special tool that empowered
them to realize their vision with as little computer clutter as possible
getting in the way. They are not inclined toward the emotionalism we see
here, but would be delighted to move back to contemporary Amiga systems.
Easy network rendering on scalable MP machines plus LightWave and CG/FX
would be back. NewTek for example, is saturated with Amigans and as they
have expressed many times on the LightWave mailing list, they would love
to have new Amiga systems to develop for.

There is probably another community - equally silent - built around
scientific visualization. Paula would probably know. In any case we are
not alone.

> If the general computing press isn't aware of what lineage of the new
> machine is, they probably wouldn't get the information right in the first
> place, and what is wrong with "It's not an Amiga.  XYZ embraces the concepts
> that created a community of zealots, but this time they did it right."

Nothing whatever. However, the computer industry has spawned firms of
highly professional information disseminators who can get the message to
those who can do the client the most good. A whole lot different than
sending off press releases - as has been the style of the Amiga stragglers
if any effort at all is made. These people personally know writers and
editors and work with them to get accurate stories in the general
computing press through actual personal contact. A major story in "Wired"
would be the equivalent of years of full page ads in the Amiga magazines
that remain. Some may sneer at the pretensions of "Wired", but it is
avidly read by a lot of well-heeled consumers who have the pocket change
to buy expensive new technology on a whim. 

> Since the new machine won't really be an Amiga in the classic sense,
> perhaps changing the name might not be a loss of anything except a
> big dose of nostolgia.  By itself, the name is not likely to draw users
> from the PC or MAC bases.  The only way you will do that is to offer
> something that is far better for the same price, or every bit as good
> for a far lower price.  But... you will still have to market it.

A new name is likely to be viewed as another Be. A system that started
development in the early '90s - a system that never gets to market. Yes,
there are people using Be, but they tend to be programmers developing
programs to show each other. Another "private label" system is not what we
need.

Having the name "Amiga" is no guarantee of success - nothing is a
guarantee of success except immense amounts of cash and marketing, and a
sterling product with game and application software better than WIntels
and Macs. Otherwise it will simply be a private label that does a
production run for us and then vanishes. If someone can come up with a
killer app, there is always a chance that it will dominate a niche and
survive - even if it does not become a contender in the Mac/PC
marketplace. Another e-mail app won't be it.

The name however, will alert folks from the Mac and PC communities that
the Amiga is back in contemporary garb. They are not so insular as you
might think. We have had many visitors from the Mac user group at AmiCUE
over the years. Of course, these are mature enthusiasts - not the bulk of
users for whom it is only a working tool.

As an aside, one visit took place by a cross section of the Mac user group
exec, to try and find out what we were doing right. At that meeting, we
had around 50 people show up - counting guests. The Mac guys were boggled
- they had over 400 members and were lucky to get 10% at any meeting. We
had about 40 members at the time - something like a 125% turnout!

larry!

-end copy-  -end copy-  -end copy-  -end copy-  -end copy-  -end copy-


        I know several that started on Amiga and went to CGI foundries, peesea
developer houses, or became mainframe programmers/controlers/adins.  Most still
have their Amiga h'ware and, I think, most would be interested in a new Amiga
with current or better features/capabilities.

        I agree with several on the TA list,  if the name can be had for
reasonable, or maybe even slightly less than reasonable, cost then I think it
would be worth it.  The highly recognizable name and badges (boing ball and/or
rainbow checkmark) would be more than worth the equivalent mucho expensive ad
work needed to push a new name.  Fleecy and Bill McEwen (Amino) are talking to
AI to see if something can be worked out.  The Phoenix group seems to be behind
them 100%.

        Meanwhile, back at the ranch...  Dirk Harlar(sp?) of the Ripper list
has stumbled across indications of a new Amiga box coming out soon.  He says
they are rolling off the assembly lines even as you read this.  Dirk is excited
as he has met with parties involved when He demoed 3.5 in Holland and saw the
signed contract.  There are low and high end boxes (ruffly equivilent to the 500
and A3/4K only with updated capabilities I assume) that should be available for
purchase in 1 or 2 months.  He has been sworn to secrecy so will not divulge
more.  Makes me want to track him down and try a lit'l bamboo-under-fingernails
therapy on him.  ;^)  I'm anxious to know the specs on these new boxes.


        _rich_        AmigaLine BBS sysop       member Team *AMIGA*





NOTICE: Last person out please turn off the light at the end of the tunnel.

Subject: [just-amiga] Gateway are b*stards!
Content-Type: text/plain
X-UIDL: 87de9eff341cf251e8dcc53142f30f19

From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

Dear all,

I have just read the news on a mainstream computer news page on
teletext on the british channel four, 21/9/99 on page 651. I am sure
you'll all know the news now and that is that Amiga will not be making
another computer but instead focus on internet applications, again,
us the community has been screwed over when everything was
going good for the first time. Groups like Digital Corruption
complained about Amiga long ago although they went about it in the
wrong way they came up with the truth long before most people could
see it.

I think we have all been wary at times but sometimes have been blind
to the facts and been living a pipe dream. Another company has
screwed us but I hope we can survive, why should now be the end?
there is nothing to pull me to the PC or Mac market so the Amiga is
still my number 1 choice and I hope you and all developers will stay
with our platform and support it, it is us who can save what we have
and no one else now. We have survived since 1993/4 until now so why
can't we carry on, I didn't see us still being here 4-5 years later
but we still are, we may have lost a few people along the way but
if in your heart of hearts you claim to be an Amiga user then stay
with us, the elite Amiga users and show the world we care about
OUR computer because now it belongs to US.

I urge Gateway to sell the rights to Amiga the company to someone
who cares and see if anyone will bid for it, they owe us this at
least, if they are going to do nothing with it then give someone
else a chance, even if no big players buy our computer name then
sell it to a smaller company and give us back the name, we don't
want to see the word Amiga on an internet box, if we'd have wanted
that we would have supported Escom.

Some may call this the 3rd time we've been done over or some might
say the second but the basic fact is its happend again and its
something we have come through before so I see no reason why
we can't do it again. The Amiga is our choice, if it wasn't the
choice of many then we wouldn't be here now, we would have
parted 3 or 4 years ago but we are the REAL users who know
our computer and like what it does and what it stands for, lets
show the computing world that we are not ready to die even if
for the future ahead we can yet see no new computer.

My pledge is to make Gateway sell the rights to Amiga to a
company of our choice that we support and we back.

I don't think we should blame Jim Collas or any Amiga worker
because I don't think this is what THEY wanted, of course not,
I blame Gateway. Tom Schmidt has been quoted as saying that
it was unrealistic, of course it isn't, the Mac is hanging around,
people are bored with the PC so it is not unrealistic at all.

They have said that they _might_ consider a licence for someone
else to work on a new computer but all this really says to me
is they believe in the back of their minds that it could take off
but they are too gutless to put a bit of effort in and give it
a go, with a licence if it doesn't take off then they are safe and
if it does they rake in the money.

I think we should all email Gateway and tell them what we really
think of them and tell them to sell the rights.

I would like to say however that I am willing to show my support
by making the commitment now that for as long as people want
AIO to keep running it will, as long as there is a small readership
then it will continue.

I would also like to say to everyone reading that I hope you
too stick with the Amiga, if you want buy a PC along side then
do that but stay with the Amiga, I for one am 100% an Amiga user
and for as long as I can see will always be. The Amiga has been
a part of my life for as long as I can remember and its not
about to die yet. Stay with us, don't let *our* computer fade away.

Toodle Pip!
-- 
Chris Seward - Editor, Amiga Information Online

Subject: [just-amiga] Tony Horgan talking out of his organ?
Content-Type: text/plain
X-UIDL: 2bf5324419fdb21eac16e903ef7ea9e3

From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>


In the latest colum in AF 129 I see Tony Horgan has split us users in
two reasons for using the computer we do, below are how he sees
each reason for using it,

- "They favour a particular application that's not available for
any other platform"

or

- "they like being part of a club"

This really is the biggest load of bulls**t i've ever heard. I do not
use my Amiga because I like one application or even 2,3 or 4 that
I could not get on a PC and then the other suggestion is just plain
taking the p**s out of us.

Neither of these reasons sum up why I personally use the Amiga.
I admit the Amiga is not as powerful as the PC but if you want a
power machine get a PC, no one is stopping you, we are here for
a reason that people can not explain and not put into words, i'm
just using my Amiga because I can. You see in the modern world,
in most countries we have a choice on what we do, what we say
and what damn computer we use. I choice Amiga because its plain
and simple I can.

I am not living in a cloud thinking that my machine is more powerful
than the latest wizz-bang PC, I agree with Tony Horgan whoever
does is mad but the reasons he says we use are Amigas are
awful.

The Amiga does 95% of what I want and the other 5% I can live with
out. Have people changed into a mode of lets slag the Amiga off
as much as possible to show we are 'funny guys' and can slag
off the computer we use? The Amiga is not like a vintage car,
we do not get pleasure from polishing it on a sunday and
occationally taking it out for a spin as heads turn. Yes, heads
probably do turn when I mention to another computer user that
I use an Amiga but it isn't a toy computer, its a serious computer.

If people used the Amiga for being part of a club then they are
not a computer user at all. I think there are a million and one
reasons we all use our Amigas, does it really matter why we
use them, the fact is we use them, the end to that story. Saying
the main two reasons are the ones he states is very narrow
minded.

Now Tony Horgan to many is seen as a good guy and i'm not
complaing about him at all, I like his work and he was one of the
best Amiga writers to past through Cu-Amiga but these few
comments are badly wrong.

So Tony Horgan, what do you like about our club or are you
here for that one application you can't find anywhere else.

Me, i'm here for the one application....

the application being....

AMIGA

Toodle Pip!

Howdy Chris

On 24-Sep-99, Chris Seward wrote:
> From: Chris Seward <amiga@thefree.net>

> My pledge is to make Gateway sell the rights to Amiga to a
> company of our choice that we support and we back.


Better idea is one I've had for a few years...
Key Word: Consortium

Sell the rights to a collective of Amiga Software and Hardware developers-
people who have PROVEN themselves and might have the combined financial
resources to pull this off.  All in the consortium would shatre both
resources, talent, and (in the end) profits, each according to their best
specialties.
  Amongst the obvious advanbtages, is that the Amiga would be protected from
the political rampages of a single company... if one outfit is tired of the
Amiga then he can pull out and still leave the others to continue it.  If
at some later date someone else wants to get in on it, he can by in and
start putting his programers/researchers/techies where his mouth is.

Have a central board- 1 rep from each company in it, but making sure that at
least half of the ones on the board are actual Engineers and one or two
knowing somethiung about marketing and the real world- to control the
allocation of resources, and then have at it.

Just think, say if Haag, Phase 5, Kruse, certain famous individuals in the
Amiga community, and maybe even Motorolla could get together (tell
motorolla they get a percentage and the freedom to get a say in how They
might want to see a real computer made- that would also elliminate the cost
for the Consortium actually #buying# the needed CPUs), what a monster
machine could be made (without the interference of politics).  Then give it
some native task emulation for PC and Mac stuff, and start advertising the
ultimate desktop supercomputer (Hey- if Apple can call their G4 a
Supercomputer with just the one chip, what do you think we could call ours
with /FOUR/ G4 chips in parallel).

It's the way it should have been done 2 or 3 companies ago.

-Later
-- 
I have made this letter longer than usual because I lack the time to
make it shorter.
-- Blaise Pascal

the same direction and prove to G2K/AI how wrong they were.  With names like
Dave Haynie, Fleecy Moos, Bill McEwen, Carl Sassenrath, Wolf Dietrich, Dan
Dodge, and many others from the Amiga h'ware and s'ware developers industry

goes, "We're mad as hell, and we're not going to take it any more".  Or as
Popeye says, "I c'n stands no more!".

        Let's do it ppl.  Let's show the corporations we will not be dictated

Dear All,

I wrote to Petro after 'the' announcement to ask some things and thought
you may want to read his reply. These are the words of Petro
Tyschtschenko.

---

Dear Chris, do not worry...Thanks for your mail......Unfortuneately I
have 
had no influence to the
 development in the last weeks.My understanding is that it is AMIGA Incs
 dream to build a ubiquitous platform that can succeed in the environment
of
 the future, not an unsuccessful computer that is rooted in the past. The
 dream of ubiquitous computing and a common amiga interface across
multiple
 devices (PC`s, Mac`s, phones, TV`s, PDA`s, cars, Internet, etc) is the
 direction of AMIGA Inc. GW wants AMIGA to be pervasive and in use by
 millions. Maybe an exciting adventure into the future. I am quite sure
that
 there are also someone enterprising people which are willing to continue
 with the existing AMIGA technology...and I will support those of course.
 I will continue to support my A 1200 sales with spareparts and service
as
 long as it is requested from our Amiga community and for the benifit of
my
 beloved AMIGA. Our Os 3.5 will be available in the next 2-3 weeks.
 
 Best regards
 Petro

---

Toodle Pip!
